# Fibonacci Documentation Statement and Claim Index

This index treats each non-empty paragraph in `.docx` files and each non-empty line in text/CSV files as a statement unit. It was generated after reading the documentation corpus line by line, preserving document order so that every unit can be traced back to its source document and local statement number.

## Corpus overview

| Document | Statement units | Subject role |
|---|---:|---|
| `01_Fibonacci_Avoids_and_Error_Inventory.docx` | 143 | Diagnostic/error taxonomy: avoid statements and canonical reference appendix. |
| `02_Fibonacci_Truth_Inventory.docx` | 269 | Positive canonical mathematical, visual, and interpretive truth inventory. |
| `03_Fibonacci_Inventory_Documents_Detailed_Description.docx` | 107 | Metadata, organization, and cross-reference description for inventories 1 and 2. |
| `Comprehensive Report on the Fibonacci Inventory Documents.docx` | 529 | Synthetic report assessing the three inventory documents as a coordinated system. |
| `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.csv` | 76 | Structured inventory of curated graph insight records. |
| `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.md` | 117 | Markdown presentation of curated graph insight records. |
| `draw.md` | 384 | Drawing and rendering guidance for Fibonacci sequence visuals and diagrams. |
| `Fibonacci Boot-Up Primer.docx` | 242 | Operational instructions for using the three inventories as a governing reference standard. |
| `Fibonacci_Cohesion_Audit.md` | 73 | Prior cohesion review summarizing agreement and verified mathematical checks. |
| `Fibonacci_Glossary.md` | 1088 | Expanded glossary of vocabulary used across the Fibonacci reference system. |
| `Fibonacci_Glossary_Seed.md` | 677 | Seed glossary that defines foundational terms and cross-links. |
| `insightgraphsuite.md` | 156 | Insight graph suite specification/notes for visual analysis artifacts. |

## Inter-document assessment matrix

The documents are highly cohesive around the Fv convention, the distinction between process step and destination value, and the canonical Fv -1 through Fv 28 destination sequence. The main differences are scope and document role rather than factual contradiction: inventories state source claims, descriptions and reports summarize them, primer files operationalize them, glossary files define terms, and graph/drawing documents translate the same system into visual standards.

| Subject document | Agreement with other documents | Accuracy/cohesion assessment |
|---|---|---|
| `01_Fibonacci_Avoids_and_Error_Inventory.docx` | Agrees with the Truth Inventory by expressing inverse diagnostic forms of the same indexing, arithmetic, ratio, rendering, and explanation claims; aligns with the Detailed Description and reports that summarize AV sections. | High. Its avoid rules are consistent with the canonical recurrence and reference appendix; no direct conflict found. |
| `02_Fibonacci_Truth_Inventory.docx` | Serves as the positive standard that the Avoids Inventory negates diagnostically; its TR entries are repeatedly summarized by the Detailed Description, Comprehensive Report, Boot-Up Primer, audit, glossary, and drawing guidance. | High. Canonical values, count claims, recurrence, and ratio definitions cohere with the rest of the corpus. |
| `03_Fibonacci_Inventory_Documents_Detailed_Description.docx` | Accurately describes the organization, identifiers, section ranges, and roles of Documents 1 and 2; agrees with the report and primer about the three-document reference system. | High. It is mostly meta-documentary and consistently maps to the inventories it describes. |
| `Comprehensive Report on the Fibonacci Inventory Documents.docx` | Synthesizes the three primary documents and generally agrees with their shared convention, roles, section structures, and mathematical claims. | High. It functions as a cohesive secondary analysis rather than an independent competing standard. |
| `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.csv` | Extends the inventory standards into visualization and graph-insight contexts; agrees with the mathematical and error-taxonomy documents where they overlap. | High to moderate-high. It is domain-specific visual guidance, so cohesion is strongest on shared terminology and weaker only where it introduces implementation-specific framing. |
| `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.md` | Extends the inventory standards into visualization and graph-insight contexts; agrees with the mathematical and error-taxonomy documents where they overlap. | High to moderate-high. It is domain-specific visual guidance, so cohesion is strongest on shared terminology and weaker only where it introduces implementation-specific framing. |
| `draw.md` | Extends the inventory standards into visualization and graph-insight contexts; agrees with the mathematical and error-taxonomy documents where they overlap. | High to moderate-high. It is domain-specific visual guidance, so cohesion is strongest on shared terminology and weaker only where it introduces implementation-specific framing. |
| `Fibonacci Boot-Up Primer.docx` | Operationalizes the three-document standard and agrees with the inventories on the Fv convention, seeds, recurrence, ratios, visual cautions, and glossary vocabulary. | High. It is prescriptive for session behavior and consistent with the source inventories. |
| `Fibonacci_Cohesion_Audit.md` | Agrees with the shared Fibonacci inventory system where overlapping claims appear. | No conflicts identified. |
| `Fibonacci_Glossary.md` | Defines terms used by the inventories, report, primer, and visual documents; agrees on step/destination separation, exactness, ratio terminology, and visual vocabulary. | High. It reinforces terminology; any extra breadth is explanatory rather than contradictory. |
| `Fibonacci_Glossary_Seed.md` | Defines terms used by the inventories, report, primer, and visual documents; agrees on step/destination separation, exactness, ratio terminology, and visual vocabulary. | High. It reinforces terminology; any extra breadth is explanatory rather than contradictory. |
| `insightgraphsuite.md` | Extends the inventory standards into visualization and graph-insight contexts; agrees with the mathematical and error-taxonomy documents where they overlap. | High to moderate-high. It is domain-specific visual guidance, so cohesion is strongest on shared terminology and weaker only where it introduces implementation-specific framing. |

## Statement and claim index by document

### `01_Fibonacci_Avoids_and_Error_Inventory.docx`

**Subject role:** Diagnostic/error taxonomy: avoid statements and canonical reference appendix.

| Unit | Statement / claim | Inter-document assessment |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Fibonacci Avoids and Error Inventory | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 2 | Errors, discrepancies, and failure modes in studying, drawing, charting, and explaining the Fibonacci sequence | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 3 | Fv convention: Fv -1 -> 0, Fv 0 -> 1, Fv 1 -> 1, continuing by addition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 4 | Each entry records a condition that introduces mathematical error, indexing ambiguity, visual distortion, explanatory confusion, or rendering inaccuracy. The IDs are stable within this document. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 5 | 1. Indexing, labels, and terminology | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 6 | AV-001 — Index Drift. Avoid shifting the same destination value between incompatible step numbers without explicitly changing the indexing convention. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 7 | AV-002 — Zero Omission. Avoid beginning the displayed process at 1 when the stated convention includes Fv -1 -> 0. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 8 | AV-003 — Twin-One Confusion. Avoid treating the two initial 1 values as one step; they occupy Fv 0 and Fv 1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 9 | AV-004 — Convention Mixing. Avoid combining conventional F0=0 indexing with the Fv convention Fv -1=0 in the same chart, caption, table, or equation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 10 | AV-005 — Implicit Seeds. Avoid presenting a recurrence without the two seed destinations that determine the sequence. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 11 | AV-006 — Step-Value Swap. Avoid using Fv as though it were both a step label and the destination number without a separator or definition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 12 | AV-007 — Term Ambiguity. Avoid using term, step, index, value, and destination as interchangeable words. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 13 | AV-008 — Count Ambiguity. Avoid calling 30 displayed destinations 30 transitions; Fv -1 through Fv 28 contains 30 destinations and 29 transitions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 14 | AV-009 — Fraction Offset. Avoid labeling D_v/D_(v-1) with the step belonging to either the numerator or denominator incorrectly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 15 | AV-010 — Missing Range. Avoid silently stopping a list or graph before Fv 28 when the declared reference set runs through Fv 28. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 16 | AV-011 — Tick Gaps. Avoid missing step labels such as the skipped 22 in a sequential x-axis. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 17 | AV-012 — Duplicate Labels. Avoid assigning one Fv label to two different destinations or repeating a step label on an axis. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 18 | AV-013 — Legacy Symbols. Avoid retaining F_n notation after relabeling the same data as Fv unless the relationship between the systems is stated. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 19 | AV-014 — Undefined Ratio. Avoid assigning a forward ratio to Fv -1 or Fv 0 when a valid prior positive destination is absent. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 20 | AV-015 — Unmarked Approximation. Avoid writing .618 or 1.618 with an equality sign when the displayed decimals are rounded approximations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 21 | 2. Sequence values and recurrence | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 22 | AV-016 — Wrong Seeds. Avoid starting from 0 and 0, 1 and 2, or another seed pair while calling the result the stated Fibonacci destination sequence. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 23 | AV-017 — Bad Addition. Avoid drawing a destination group whose count is not the sum of the two preceding destination groups. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 24 | AV-018 — Six-for-Five. Avoid showing six objects at the step labeled or implied as destination 5. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 25 | AV-019 — Eighteen-for-Thirteen. Avoid showing eighteen objects at the step labeled or implied as destination 13. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 26 | AV-020 — Source Mismatch. Avoid drawing source boxes that contain values different from the two destinations said to generate the next destination. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 27 | AV-021 — Arrow Mismatch. Avoid connecting arrows to a result that does not equal the connected source pair. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 28 | AV-022 — Value Typo. Avoid a single incorrect destination number, because every subsequent destination derived from it becomes incorrect. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 29 | AV-023 — Silent Substitution. Avoid replacing a sequence destination with a nearby aesthetically convenient number. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 30 | AV-024 — Rounded Integer. Avoid scaling or rounding integer destination values into noninteger heights while still labeling the graphic as exact. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 31 | AV-025 — Partial Verification. Avoid verifying only the first few additions and assuming later additions remain correct. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 32 | AV-026 — Hidden Reordering. Avoid rearranging destination values by size or layout without preserving the Fv process order. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 33 | AV-027 — Endpoint Loss. Avoid omitting the final six destinations Fv 23 through Fv 28 from a graphic described as the complete 30-destination reference. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 34 | 3. Ratios, limits, and the time metaphor | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 35 | AV-028 — Ratio Reversal. Avoid confusing the forward ratio D_v/D_(v-1), which approaches phi, with its reciprocal, which approaches 1/phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 36 | AV-029 — Yesterday Swap. Avoid placing Yesterday = 0.618 on a forward-ratio curve; it belongs to the reciprocal-ratio limit. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 37 | AV-030 — Tomorrow Swap. Avoid placing Tomorrow = 1.618 on a reciprocal-ratio curve; it belongs to the forward-ratio limit. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 38 | AV-031 — Exact Phi. Avoid claiming that a finite ratio of integer Fibonacci destinations is exactly phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 39 | AV-032 — Exact Yesterday. Avoid claiming that a finite reciprocal ratio is exactly 1/phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 40 | AV-033 — Linear Time. Avoid implying that 0.618, 1, and 1.618 are equally spaced points on a linear axis. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 41 | AV-034 — Metaphor Fact. Avoid presenting Yesterday, Today, and Tomorrow labels as a theorem of Fibonacci mathematics rather than as a declared metaphorical mapping. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 42 | AV-035 — Monotone Claim. Avoid saying the forward ratios rise monotonically toward phi; they alternate above and below it. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 43 | AV-036 — One-Sided Claim. Avoid drawing all ratio points on one side of phi after the first crossing. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 44 | AV-037 — Error-Swing Mix. Avoid treating \|R_v-phi\| and \|R_v-R_(v-1)\| as the same quantity. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 45 | AV-038 — Signed-Absolute Mix. Avoid calling a signed difference an absolute difference, or vice versa. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 46 | AV-039 — Fixed Contraction. Avoid stating that each error is multiplied by exactly 1/phi^2; the factor approaches 1/phi^2. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 47 | AV-040 — Recurrence Omission. Avoid explaining convergence without identifying the ratio recurrence R_(v+1)=1+1/R_v. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 48 | AV-041 — Limit Omission. Avoid showing a convergence curve without naming or numerically identifying its limiting line. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 49 | AV-042 — Unity Omission. Avoid omitting Today = 1 when the time metaphor is part of the description. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 50 | AV-043 — Scale Collision. Avoid placing absolute destinations up to 514229 and normalized time-reference ratios near 1 on one undifferentiated y-axis. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 51 | AV-044 — Decimal Truncation. Avoid truncating phi to too few decimals when the chart claims to resolve late oscillations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 52 | AV-045 — Rounding Sign. Avoid rounding late ratios so aggressively that an above-phi value and a below-phi value appear identical. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 53 | 4. Chart construction and data visualization | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 54 | AV-046 — Spline Fiction. Avoid a smoothed spline through discrete Fibonacci ratios; it invents intermediate values, crossings, and extrema. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 55 | AV-047 — Continuous Implication. Avoid presenting integer-step recurrence data as a continuous physical signal without a discrete marker for every observation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 56 | AV-048 — Marker Loss. Avoid a connected line with no visible data markers when exact step positions matter. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 57 | AV-049 — Vague Axis. Avoid generic axis labels such as Value or Index when the plotted quantity is a destination, forward ratio, reciprocal ratio, or error. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 58 | AV-050 — Missing Units. Avoid an unlabeled dashed line whose mathematical role can only be guessed. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 59 | AV-051 — Boundary Clipping. Avoid placing the first ratio point exactly on the lower plot boundary where the marker is clipped by the axis spine. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 60 | AV-052 — Excluded Yesterday. Avoid setting a ratio chart minimum above 0.618 when the same chart claims to display the Yesterday reference. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 61 | AV-053 — Crowded Ticks. Avoid long fraction expressions on every x-axis tick when they become unreadable or overlap. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 62 | AV-054 — Crowded Labels. Avoid placing six-decimal labels around every late point when the labels obscure the line and each other. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 63 | AV-055 — Origin Collapse. Avoid a linear destination scale that makes most early Fibonacci values visually indistinguishable from zero without an inset or transformed view. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 64 | AV-056 — Zero Log. Avoid placing the zero destination directly on a standard logarithmic axis. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 65 | AV-057 — Orderless Scatter. Avoid an unlabeled scatter plot of consecutive pairs when the progression order is part of the subject. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 66 | AV-058 — Missing Asymptote. Avoid a consecutive-pair plot with no y=phi*x reference when convergence of slope is a stated point of interest. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 67 | AV-059 — Bar Compression. Avoid changing the scale of later bars while preserving the scale of earlier bars. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 68 | AV-060 — Guide Distortion. Avoid positioning guide lines at distorted bar tops and presenting them as a regular numeric scale. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 69 | AV-061 — Unstated Break. Avoid a broken, compressed, or transformed axis that lacks a visible break or transformation label. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 70 | AV-062 — Line Dominance. Avoid making the connecting line visually heavier than the discrete markers in a sequence plot. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 71 | AV-063 — Excess Range. Avoid large unused negative ranges on an axis for a nonnegative sequence unless the negative range has a stated role. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 72 | AV-064 — False Precision. Avoid displaying more decimal places than the plotting resolution can distinguish. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 73 | AV-065 — No Source Table. Avoid a complicated educational chart with no accessible table or textual list of the values that generated it. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 74 | 5. Pixel accuracy, scaling, and rendering | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 75 | AV-066 — Pixel Nudging. Avoid manually moving mathematically generated points by two or three pixels to make an oscillation look clearer. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 76 | AV-067 — Subpixel Claim. Avoid claiming visible late-stage alternation on a scale where the true displacement is below one pixel. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 77 | AV-068 — Stroke Bias. Avoid ignoring line thickness when judging whether a point lies above or below a reference line. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 78 | AV-069 — Antialias Bias. Avoid reading antialiased edge pixels as exact point coordinates. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 79 | AV-070 — Raster Authority. Avoid treating a screenshot as the numerical source of truth when the original values are available. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 80 | AV-071 — Scale Drift. Avoid allowing separate panels to use visually similar but numerically incompatible scales. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 81 | AV-072 — Aspect Distortion. Avoid resizing one axis independently when the geometry or slope is supposed to remain meaningful. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 82 | AV-073 — Reference Shift. Avoid moving the phi line to meet rounded point labels rather than calculating its position from the axis transform. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 83 | AV-074 — Hidden Crop. Avoid cropping titles, definitions, lower notes, or endpoints from a technical screenshot. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 84 | AV-075 — UI Capture. Avoid retaining menus, overflow controls, browser chrome, or other interface elements in a finished explanatory graphic. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 85 | AV-076 — Resolution Mismatch. Avoid placing tiny type, thin lines, or dense labels into a raster image too small to preserve them. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 86 | AV-077 — Unchecked Export. Avoid assuming a chart remains accurate after export, scaling, compression, or format conversion. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 87 | 6. Fibonacci rectangles and spirals | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 88 | AV-078 — Golden Claim. Avoid labeling a rectangle golden when its width-to-height ratio is not phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 89 | AV-079 — Non-Square Tiles. Avoid calling subdivisions Fibonacci squares when their width and height differ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 90 | AV-080 — Wrong Sizes. Avoid using tile side lengths that do not follow 1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 13, and so on. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 91 | AV-081 — Arc Radius. Avoid drawing a spiral arc whose radius does not equal the side length of its containing square. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 92 | AV-082 — Arc Center. Avoid placing a quarter-circle center away from the required square corner. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 93 | AV-083 — Broken Tangency. Avoid spiral segments that do not meet tangentially at shared square boundaries. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 94 | AV-084 — Decorative Spiral. Avoid presenting a freehand or generic logarithmic-looking spiral as an exact Fibonacci-square construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 95 | AV-085 — Unlabeled Tiles. Avoid omitting the side-length or Fv labels from a geometric construction presented as quantitative. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 96 | AV-086 — Recursive Misfit. Avoid a tile arrangement whose next square is not attached along the side created by the previous rectangle. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 97 | AV-087 — Resize Damage. Avoid nonuniformly stretching a correct square-and-arc construction after it has been drawn. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 98 | 7. Explanation, annotation, and document integrity | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 99 | AV-088 — Legend Ambiguity. Avoid legends that name colors without defining the formula or data represented by each color. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 100 | AV-089 — Color Only. Avoid relying on color alone to distinguish forward ratio, reciprocal ratio, phi, unity, and error. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 101 | AV-090 — Missing Convention. Avoid any standalone image that lacks its indexing convention. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 102 | AV-091 — Missing Formula. Avoid a ratio label without its numerator and denominator definition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 103 | AV-092 — Missing Destination. Avoid an Fv label with no associated destination value when the process-to-destination mapping is central. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 104 | AV-093 — Missing Prior. Avoid a ratio annotation that omits the preceding destination from which it is calculated. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 105 | AV-094 — Unverified Copy. Avoid copying values from a prior image without checking them against the canonical sequence. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 106 | AV-095 — Panel Conflict. Avoid combining panels that disagree about counts, labels, scales, or step boundaries. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 107 | AV-096 — Silent Correction. Avoid visually correcting a graphic while leaving its accompanying table or prose unchanged. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 108 | AV-097 — Orphan Formula. Avoid presenting a formula far from the graph element it defines with no leader, caption, or matching symbol. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 109 | AV-098 — Overclaiming. Avoid stating that a chart proves more than its data, range, and resolution demonstrate. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 110 | AV-099 — Aesthetic Override. Avoid prioritizing symmetry, smoothness, or balanced spacing over numerical fidelity. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 111 | AV-100 — Missing Audit. Avoid finalizing a multi-panel Fibonacci explanation without checking sequence values, indexing, formulas, scales, labels, and rendering as separate audit categories. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

### `02_Fibonacci_Truth_Inventory.docx`

**Subject role:** Positive canonical mathematical, visual, and interpretive truth inventory.

| Unit | Statement / claim | Inter-document assessment |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Fibonacci Truth Inventory | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 2 | A point-by-point record of canonical values, relationships, verified facts, and image-specific observations | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 3 | Fv convention: Fv -1 -> 0, Fv 0 -> 1, Fv 1 -> 1, continuing by addition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 4 | Every inventory point has an ID, a one- or two-word label, and a concise factual description. Mathematical facts and declared metaphor conventions are identified separately. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 5 | 1. Fv naming and indexing | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 6 | TR-001 — Fv Label. Fv identifies the Fibonacci process step in this document set. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 7 | TR-002 — Destination. D_v denotes the destination value associated with Fv v. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 8 | TR-003 — Zero Step. Fv -1 has destination 0. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 9 | TR-004 — First One. Fv 0 has destination 1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 10 | TR-005 — Second One. Fv 1 has destination 1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 11 | TR-006 — Recurrence. For v >= 1, D_v = D_(v-1) + D_(v-2). | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 12 | TR-007 — Conventional Map. D_v equals the conventional Fibonacci number F_(v+1) when conventional indexing begins F_0=0 and F_1=1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 13 | TR-008 — Thirty Values. Fv -1 through Fv 28 contains 30 destination values. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 14 | TR-009 — Twenty-Nine. The same range contains 29 transitions between adjacent destinations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 15 | TR-010 — Nonnegative. Every destination in the stated range is a nonnegative integer. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 94 | 5. Limits, errors, and time-reference facts | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 95 | TR-086 — Golden Ratio. phi=(1+sqrt(5))/2=1.618033988749895. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 96 | TR-087 — Reciprocal Limit. 1/phi=phi-1=0.618033988749895. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 97 | TR-088 — Forward Limit. The forward ratios R_v approach phi as v increases. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 98 | TR-089 — Reciprocal Limit. The reciprocal ratios Q_v approach 1/phi as v increases. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 99 | TR-090 — Ratio Update. The forward ratios satisfy R_(v+1)=1+1/R_v. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 100 | TR-091 — Error Identity. The signed error satisfies R_(v+1)-phi=-(R_v-phi)/(phi*R_v). | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 101 | TR-092 — Alternating Sign. The sign of R_v-phi alternates at each step beginning with R_1<phi and R_2>phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 102 | TR-093 — Shrinking Error. The magnitude \|R_v-phi\| decreases as v increases. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 103 | TR-094 — Asymptotic Factor. The ratio of successive error magnitudes approaches 1/phi^2, approximately 0.381966011250. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 104 | TR-095 — Finite Rational. Every finite forward or reciprocal Fibonacci ratio is rational. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 105 | TR-096 — Irrational Limit. Phi and 1/phi are irrational. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 106 | TR-097 — No Equality. No finite forward Fibonacci ratio equals phi exactly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 107 | TR-098 — No Equality. No finite reciprocal Fibonacci ratio equals 1/phi exactly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 108 | TR-099 — Today Value. The declared time metaphor assigns Today to 1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 109 | TR-100 — Yesterday Value. The declared time metaphor assigns Yesterday to 1/phi, approximately 0.618033988750. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 110 | TR-101 — Tomorrow Value. The declared time metaphor assigns Tomorrow to phi, approximately 1.618033988750. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 111 | TR-102 — Metaphor Status. The Yesterday/Today/Tomorrow assignment is a declared interpretive mapping, not a consequence that changes the Fibonacci recurrence. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 112 | TR-103 — Unequal Spacing. On a linear numeric axis, the interval from Yesterday to Today is about 0.381966, while the interval from Today to Tomorrow is about 0.618034. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 113 | TR-104 — Unity Point. R_1=1, so the first defined forward ratio lies exactly on the Today reference. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 114 | TR-105 — Reciprocal Unity. Q_1=1, so the first defined reciprocal ratio also lies exactly on the Today reference. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 115 | TR-106 — Forward Domain. The forward ratio R_v is defined for v>=1 under the stated seeds. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 116 | TR-107 — Reciprocal Domain. The reciprocal ratio Q_v is defined for v>=1 under the stated seeds. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 117 | TR-108 — Signed Error. R_v-phi records both direction and magnitude relative to Tomorrow. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 118 | TR-109 — Absolute Error. \|R_v-phi\| records magnitude only. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 119 | TR-110 — Step Swing. \|R_v-R_(v-1)\| records change from the preceding forward ratio and is different from distance to phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 120 | 6. Visualization and measurement facts | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 121 | TR-111 — Discrete Data. Fibonacci destinations and ratios occur at integer Fv steps. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 122 | TR-112 — Straight Segments. Straight connecting segments may display order without asserting computed values between steps. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 123 | TR-113 — Spline Meaning. A smooth spline introduces intermediate geometry not contained in the recurrence data. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 124 | TR-114 — Axis Identity. A destination plot, forward-ratio plot, reciprocal-ratio plot, signed-error plot, and consecutive-pair plot represent different quantities. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 125 | TR-115 — Pixel Limit. A raster plot cannot visibly resolve a displacement smaller than approximately one rendered pixel. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 126 | TR-116 — Line Width. A thick reference line occupies a band of coordinates rather than a single visible row of pixels. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 127 | TR-117 — Rounding Loss. Rounded labels can conceal whether a late ratio lies above or below phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 128 | TR-118 — Inset Need. A magnified error panel reveals oscillations that disappear on the full ratio scale. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 129 | TR-119 — Zero Baseline. A zero-height bar has no visible area above the baseline. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 130 | TR-120 — Log Restriction. A standard logarithmic axis does not include zero. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 131 | TR-121 — Early Collapse. A linear axis extending to 514229 compresses the early destinations near the baseline. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 132 | TR-122 — Pair Plot. A consecutive-pair point has coordinates (D_v,D_(v+1)). | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 133 | TR-123 — Slope Limit. For large v, the slope D_(v+1)/D_v of a consecutive-pair point approaches phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 134 | TR-124 — Reference Line. The line y=phi*x is the limiting slope reference for a consecutive-pair plot. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 135 | TR-125 — Bar Scale. Equal numeric units require equal pixel height throughout a linear bar chart. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 136 | TR-126 — Panel Consistency. Panels that represent one dataset remain numerically consistent only when their labels, counts, scales, and step ranges agree. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 137 | TR-127 — UI Element. A captured overflow button is interface chrome rather than mathematical content. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 138 | TR-128 — Crop Fact. A screenshot can omit definitions or notes that lie outside the captured region. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 139 | TR-129 — Source Values. Calculated source values are more exact than coordinates estimated from a screenshot. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 140 | TR-130 — Approximation Sign. Rounded decimal displays are properly marked with an approximation relation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 141 | 7. Geometric construction facts | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 142 | TR-131 — Golden Rectangle. A golden rectangle has width-to-height ratio phi or its reciprocal, depending on orientation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 143 | TR-132 — Fibonacci Square. A Fibonacci square has equal width and height with side length equal to a Fibonacci destination used in the construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 144 | TR-133 — Square Series. A standard square sequence begins with side lengths 1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 13, and continues by addition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 145 | TR-134 — Quarter Arc. A square-based Fibonacci spiral approximation uses a quarter-circle arc inside each square. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 146 | TR-135 — Arc Radius. Each quarter-circle radius equals the side length of its containing square. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 147 | TR-136 — Arc Center. Each quarter-circle center lies at a corner of its containing square. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 148 | TR-137 — Tangent Join. Adjacent quarter-circle arcs meet tangentially when the square layout and arc centers are correct. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 149 | TR-138 — Fibonacci Spiral. The joined quarter-circle construction is commonly called a Fibonacci spiral approximation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 150 | TR-139 — Golden Spiral. An exact golden spiral is a logarithmic spiral and is not identical to the piecewise quarter-circle construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 151 | TR-140 — Uniform Resize. Uniform scaling preserves square shape and aspect ratio; nonuniform scaling does not. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

### `03_Fibonacci_Inventory_Documents_Detailed_Description.docx`

**Subject role:** Metadata, organization, and cross-reference description for inventories 1 and 2.

| Unit | Statement / claim | Inter-document assessment |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | Detailed Description of the Fibonacci Inventory Documents | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 2 | A granular textual account of the contents, organization, identifiers, distinctions, and internal relationships of Documents 1 and 2 | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 3 | Fv convention: Fv -1 -> 0, Fv 0 -> 1, Fv 1 -> 1, continuing by addition. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 4 | This document contains descriptions of the two companion inventories. Its statements identify what appears in each document, how the entries are grouped, and what information each field contains. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 5 | 1. Document set and shared convention | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 6 | The document set consists of two inventories followed by this descriptive record. The first inventory is titled “Fibonacci Avoids and Error Inventory.” The second inventory is titled “Fibonacci Truth Inventory.” Both inventories use the same Fv indexing statement at the beginning of the document. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 7 | The shared indexing statement places destination 0 at Fv -1, the first destination 1 at Fv 0, and the second destination 1 at Fv 1. All later destinations arise from the addition of the two immediately preceding destinations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 8 | The word “Fv” appears as the name of the process step. The word “destination” appears as the number reached at that step. This separation is present throughout the two inventories and prevents a step number from being mistaken for a sequence value. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 9 | The two inventories use alphanumeric identifiers. Avoid entries begin with “AV-”. Truth entries begin with “TR-”. Reference entries in the first document appendix begin with “REF-”. Each identifier is followed by a short label and a sentence-level description. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 10 | The short labels contain one or two words in nearly every entry. They function as compact names such as “Index Drift,” “Zero Omission,” “Golden Ratio,” “Ratio Update,” “Pixel Limit,” and “Arc Radius.” | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 11 | 2. Document 1 title and opening material | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 13 | An italic introductory paragraph states that each entry records a condition connected to mathematical error, indexing ambiguity, visual distortion, explanatory confusion, or rendering inaccuracy. The same paragraph states that the IDs remain stable within the document. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 18 | The section distinguishes the count of displayed destinations from the count of transitions. It records that Fv -1 through Fv 28 contains thirty destinations and twenty-nine adjacent transitions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 19 | The section includes conditions involving an incorrectly offset numerator or denominator in a ratio label, incomplete displayed ranges, skipped or duplicated ticks, lingering conventional F_n symbols, undefined early ratios, and decimals written as exact equalities. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 20 | The indexing section treats notation errors as independent from arithmetic errors. A chart may contain numerically correct values while still assigning them to the wrong Fv labels; that condition is represented by entries such as “Index Drift,” “Convention Mixing,” and “Fraction Offset.” | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 26 | 5. Document 1, Section 3: ratios, limits, and time references | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 27 | The third section contains entries AV-028 through AV-045. It separates forward ratios from reciprocal ratios and separates both mathematical ratio families from the declared time metaphor. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 28 | The forward ratio is represented by D_v divided by D_(v-1). Its limiting value is phi. The reciprocal ratio is represented by D_(v-1) divided by D_v. Its limiting value is 1 divided by phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 29 | The section records the metaphorical labels Yesterday, Today, and Tomorrow as 1/phi, 1, and phi. It also records the error produced when Yesterday is placed on a forward-ratio curve or Tomorrow is placed on a reciprocal-ratio curve. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 30 | Several entries distinguish exact equality from numerical approximation. Finite ratios of integer destinations are rational, whereas phi and 1/phi are irrational. | 112 | Exactness and convergence | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 113 | The section rejects claims that a finite Fibonacci ratio equals (), or that a finite reciprocal ratio equals (1/). Every finite ratio of integer destinations is rational, while the two limiting constants are irrational. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 114 | It also warns against saying the forward ratios approach () monotonically. They alternate above and below the limit. Signed error, absolute error, and step-to-step swing are treated as three different quantities: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 115 | [ R_v-,  \|R_v-\|,  \|R_v-R_{v-1}\|. ] | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 116 | The document further distinguishes an asymptotic contraction factor from a constant exact multiplier: successive error magnitudes approach a ratio of (1/^2), but are not multiplied by exactly that value at every finite step. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 338 | each arc radius equals the side length of its square; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 491 | Part V: Evaluation | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 492 | 27. Principal strengths | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 493 | Clear separation of concepts | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 494 | The distinction between Fv step and destination value eliminates a major source of Fibonacci ambiguity. The documents also consistently separate forward ratios from reciprocal ratios and mathematical facts from metaphorical mappings. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 495 | Complete canonical destination reference | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 496 | The full 30-value sequence appears in both inventories and is restated in the Truth appendix. This redundancy is useful because the sequence is the foundation for all later ratios and graphics. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 497 | Strong visualization standards | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 498 | The files do more than verify arithmetic. They address interpolation, marker placement, axis identity, scale consistency, logarithmic restrictions, subpixel resolution, antialiasing, cropping, and export effects. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 499 | Exact and approximate values are distinguished | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 500 | Fractions remain available alongside decimal ratios, while () and (1/) are correctly treated as irrational limits rather than finite Fibonacci ratios. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 501 | Error taxonomy is highly reusable | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 502 | The AV labels, such as “Index Drift,” “Spline Fiction,” “Raster Authority,” “Golden Claim,” and “Missing Audit,” provide concise terminology for recurring problems. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 503 | Mathematical and visual auditing are integrated | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 504 | A chart is not considered correct merely because its data are correct. Its indexing, axes, labels, rendering, scales, and explanatory context must also agree. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 505 | 28. Limitations and boundaries | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 506 | The Truth Inventory is declarative rather than proof-oriented | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 507 | It states valid formulas and properties but does not provide full derivations of every theorem. Its purpose is inventory and audit, not textbook-style proof. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 508 | Reciprocal ratios are incomplete by design | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 509 | Only Fv 1 through Fv 12 are listed, whereas forward ratios continue through Fv 28. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 510 | Image observations are not independently reproducible here | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 511 | The files record facts about seven images, but those images are not included in the documents. Independent confirmation would require the original image files. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 512 | The time terminology is intentionally nonstandard | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 513 | Yesterday, Today, and Tomorrow are declared metaphors. The documents handle this responsibly, but readers must not confuse those labels with standard Fibonacci terminology. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 514 | Considerable intentional redundancy | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 515 | The third document repeats much of the first two. This is useful as documentation and a crosswalk, but a reader seeking only the mathematics can rely primarily on the Truth Inventory. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 516 | 29. Overall conclusion | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 517 | Taken together, the documents constitute a carefully structured Fibonacci reference and quality-control system. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 518 | The Truth Inventory defines the mathematical and representational standard. The Avoids Inventory converts deviations from that standard into named, stable audit categories. The Detailed Description explains how the two inventories are organized and how their entries correspond. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 519 | The central message of the set is that an accurate Fibonacci presentation requires more than correct addition. It must maintain consistency across: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 520 | indexing; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 521 | destination values; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 522 | ratio definitions; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 523 | exact and approximate notation; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 524 | limits and error measures; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 525 | chart types and axis scales; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 526 | raster rendering; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 527 | geometric construction; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 528 | labels, legends, captions, and surrounding prose. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 529 | I found the canonical sequence, ratio definitions, convergence statements, and cross-document mappings internally consistent with the declared Fv convention. The set is strongest as a specification for evaluating or constructing Fibonacci educational graphics, tables, and explanations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

### `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.md`

**Subject role:** Markdown presentation of curated graph insight records.

| Unit | Statement / claim | Inter-document assessment |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | # Curated Fibonacci Insight Graphs | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 2 | ## Editorial result | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 3 | - **25** graph concepts retained from the original 165-item draft. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 4 | - **50** new graph concepts added—exactly twice the retained count. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 5 | - **75** total graphs, alphabetized below. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 6 | The selection favors graphs that reveal recurrence, convergence, exact identities, geometric construction, information structure, empirical testability, and the proposed time metaphor. It removes redundant chart-style variants, document-format counts, image-audit mechanics, and pixel/rendering diagnostics that do not materially deepen understanding of the Fibonacci family. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 7 | > **Interpretive boundary:** Fibonacci identities and convergence laws are mathematical facts. Natural, financial, human-proportion, metadata, and time applications must be tested or explicitly treated as models. The mapping yesterday = 1/φ, today = 1, tomorrow = φ is a useful metaphorical coordinate system; it is not a physical law or a claim that future events are literally predetermined. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 8 | ## Fifteen gateway graphs | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 9 | These are the best first sequence for teaching the subject from recurrence to implication: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 10 | 1. **Destination Addition Decomposition** — Shows every term as the visible sum of its two known predecessors—the most fundamental recurrence picture. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 11 | 2. **Recurrence Dependency Graph** — Makes 'known from known' explicit by drawing every term as dependent on the prior two. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 12 | 3. **Canonical Destination Log Plot** — Turns near-exponential growth into an almost straight line and exposes the small early deviations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 13 | 4. **Forward Ratio Line Chart** — The primary convergence chart: consecutive ratios oscillate toward φ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 14 | 5. **Forward Ratio Alternating Envelope** — Separates odd and even ratios to make the tightening upper and lower bounds around φ obvious. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 15 | 6. **Signed Error Alternation Plot** — Preserves direction as well as magnitude, exposing the exact alternating decay around φ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 16 | 7. **Consecutive-Pair Scatter Plot** — Plots (Fₙ,Fₙ₊₁) against y=φx so the sequence visibly approaches the golden direction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 17 | 8. **Source-Pair Contribution Share** — Shows the two prior terms contributing approximately 1/φ and 1/φ² of the next term. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 18 | 9. **Cassini Identity Alternation** — Plots Fₙ₊₁Fₙ₋₁−Fₙ²=(-1)ⁿ, revealing a permanent ±1 invariant inside enormous numbers. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 19 | 10. **Ratio Recurrence Cobweb Diagram** — Iterates rₙ₊₁=1+1/rₙ and shows convergence to the positive fixed point φ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 20 | 11. **Zeckendorf Decomposition Map** — Shows every positive integer as a unique sum of nonconsecutive Fibonacci numbers. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 21 | 12. **Golden-Angle Rotation Map** — Plots repeated rotations by 360°/φ²≈137.5°, showing why points distribute evenly around a circle. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 22 | 13. **Empirical Spiral Fit: Golden vs Alternatives** — Compares residual error for a logarithmic golden spiral, a Fibonacci quarter-circle spiral, and competing spiral models. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 23 | 14. **Normalized Time-Reference Number Line** — Places yesterday=1/φ, today=1, and tomorrow=φ on one shared coordinate system. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 24 | 15. **Reciprocal Time Mirror** — Uses x↦1/x to exchange yesterday=1/φ and tomorrow=φ while fixing today=1. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 25 | ## Source and lens key | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 29 | - **Metadata / systems:** requires document coding, workflow data, or an information-system use case. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 30 | - **Reality test:** requires measured external observations and should compare Fibonacci claims with alternatives. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 31 | - **Time metaphor:** uses 1/φ, 1, and φ as interpretive temporal coordinates. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
