| 722 | ### False Precision | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 723 | - **Definition:** Displaying more decimal places than the plotting resolution can distinguish. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 724 | - **Role/domain:** Visualization; exactness error. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 725 | - **Caution:** Numerical labels should not imply visual certainty beyond the chart's resolution. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 726 | - **Identifiers:** AV-064; Pixel Limit TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 727 | ### No Source Table | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 728 | - **Definition:** A complex educational chart lacking an accessible table or textual list of its source values. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 729 | - **Role/domain:** Visualization; auditability. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 730 | - **Caution:** Without source data, chart values are hard to verify. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 731 | - **Identifiers:** AV-065; Source Values TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 732 | ## F. Pixel accuracy, scaling, rendering, and export | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 733 | ### Pixel accuracy | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 734 | - **Definition:** The degree to which raster pixels can represent exact mathematical positions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 735 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering; measurement. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 736 | - **Caution:** Pixel displays have finite resolution and cannot establish subpixel claims by sight alone. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 737 | - **Identifiers:** AV-066--AV-077; Pixel Limit TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 738 | ### Pixel Limit | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 739 | - **Definition:** The Truth Inventory principle that pixel resolution limits what can be visually distinguished. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 740 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering; visualization. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 741 | - **Caution:** Do not claim visible late-stage alternation below one pixel of displacement. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 742 | - **Identifiers:** Pixel Limit TR entry; AV-067. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 743 | ### Pixel Nudging | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 744 | - **Definition:** Manually moving mathematically generated points by a few pixels to make an oscillation clearer. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 745 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering error; data integrity. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 746 | - **Caution:** It sacrifices source-data fidelity for appearance. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 747 | - **Identifiers:** AV-066; AV-099. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 748 | ### Subpixel Claim | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 749 | - **Definition:** Claiming a visible distinction when the true displacement is below one pixel. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 750 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering error. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 751 | - **Caution:** Use calculated values or an error/inset panel instead. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 752 | - **Identifiers:** AV-067; Pixel Limit and Inset Need TR entries. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 753 | ### Stroke Bias | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 754 | - **Definition:** Ignoring line thickness when judging whether a plotted point lies above or below a reference line. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 755 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering caution. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 756 | - **Caution:** The stroke can overlap the reference even when the mathematical point is on one side. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 757 | - **Identifiers:** AV-068; Line Width TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 758 | ### Antialias Bias | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 759 | - **Definition:** Reading antialiased edge pixels as exact coordinates. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 760 | - **Role/domain:** Rendering caution. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 763 | ### Raster Authority | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 766 | - **Caution:** Prefer source values over screenshot measurement. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 768 | ### Scale Drift | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 773 | ### Aspect Distortion | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 778 | ### Reference Shift | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 779 | - **Definition:** Moving the phi line to meet rounded point labels rather than calculating its position from the axis transform. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 803 | ## G. Fibonacci rectangles, squares, and spirals | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 811 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry; ratio. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 812 | - **Caution:** Verify aspect ratio; visual resemblance is insufficient. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 814 | ### Golden Claim | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 815 | - **Definition:** Labeling a rectangle golden when its width-to-height ratio is not phi. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 816 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry error. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 817 | - **Caution:** Approximate Fibonacci rectangles may approach but are not necessarily exact golden rectangles. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 819 | ### Fibonacci Square | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 820 | - **Definition:** A square tile in a Fibonacci construction whose side length follows the Fibonacci side-length series. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 822 | - **Caution:** Width and height must be equal. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 825 | - **Definition:** The side-length series `1, 1, 2, 3, 5, 8, 13, ...` used for Fibonacci-square constructions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 826 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry; recurrence. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 827 | - **Caution:** Wrong side lengths invalidate the construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 829 | ### Non-Square Tiles | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 830 | - **Definition:** Calling subdivisions Fibonacci squares when their width and height differ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 834 | ### Quarter Arc | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 835 | - **Definition:** A quarter-circle segment drawn inside a Fibonacci square with radius equal to that square's side length. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 836 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry; spiral construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 837 | - **Caution:** Radius and center must match the containing square. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 839 | ### Arc Radius | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 840 | - **Definition:** The radius of a spiral arc, required to equal the side length of its containing square in the Fibonacci-square construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 841 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry requirement. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 842 | - **Caution:** A mismatched radius breaks the construction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 843 | - **Identifiers:** AV-081; Quarter Arc TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 844 | ### Arc Center | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 845 | - **Definition:** The required square corner from which a quarter-circle arc is drawn. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 846 | - **Role/domain:** Geometry requirement. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 847 | - **Caution:** Moving the center away from the correct corner invalidates the arc geometry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 848 | - **Identifiers:** AV-082; Quarter Arc TR entry. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 849 | ### Tangent Join / Broken Tangency | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 850 | - **Definition:** Adjacent quarter-circle arcs should meet tangentially; broken tangency is failure to do so at shared square boundaries. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 852 | - **Caution:** Smooth-looking arcs are not sufficient if centers, radii, or joins are wrong. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 960 | ## I. Image-specific observations and evidence boundaries | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 961 | ### Uploaded images / seven examined images | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 962 | - **Definition:** The images whose properties were recorded in the Truth Inventory when the inventories were created. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 963 | - **Role/domain:** Image audit; document scope. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 964 | - **Caution:** Their observations are facts about those images only, not automatic judgments about new images. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 965 | - **Identifiers:** TR image-specific observation section. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 966 | ### Image One: dark screenshot | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 967 | - **Definition:** A previously examined dark screenshot associated with ratio recurrence, signed-error identity, asymptotic contraction, and conventional indexing display. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 968 | - **Role/domain:** Image-specific observation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 969 | - **Caution:** Treat as image-specific and do not generalize without re-auditing a new image. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 1087 | ## Audit-use note | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 1088 | Use this glossary as a navigation aid alongside the governing documents. For correctness, check positive facts against the **Truth Inventory**, classify deviations with the **Avoids Inventory**, consult the **Detailed Description** for identifier namespaces and document organization, and use the **Comprehensive Report** for high-level synthesis and known limitations. In every audit, preserve the Fv convention, keep process steps distinct from destination values, maintain exact fractions and symbolic constants where exactness matters, mark rounded decimals as approximations, and avoid claiming that any finite Fibonacci ratio equals phi or `1/phi` exactly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

| 664 | ## Step 1 — Fresh-session prompt for writing the full glossary | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 665 | Use the following prompt in a new LLM session: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 666 | ```text | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 667 | You are starting a fresh session in the repository containing the Fibonacci inventory documents. Before writing anything substantive, read every document in the repository, then execute the “Fibonacci Boot-Up Primer” exactly: study and comprehend the governing Fibonacci Avoids and Error Inventory, Fibonacci Truth Inventory, and Detailed Description of the Fibonacci Inventory Documents as one unified reference system, while also reading the Comprehensive Report and this Fibonacci_Glossary_Seed.md document. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 668 | After boot-up, write a full glossary from the raw seed list in Fibonacci_Glossary_Seed.md. Do not merely alphabetize terms mechanically. Build a careful glossary that defines each vocabulary word or specialized phrase according to the document set, preserves the Fv convention, distinguishes Fv process steps from destination values, distinguishes TR truths from AV error conditions and REF canonical references, and clearly separates exact mathematical facts, document-defined conventions, visualization standards, rendering cautions, geometric construction requirements, image-specific observations, and external mathematical context. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 669 | For every glossary entry, include: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 670 | 1. the term or phrase; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 671 | 2. a concise definition faithful to the documents; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 672 | 3. its role or domain, such as indexing, recurrence, ratio, convergence, metaphor, visualization, rendering, geometry, image audit, document structure, or workflow; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 673 | 4. any important caution, especially if the documents warn against confusing it with another term; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 674 | 5. relevant AV, TR, or REF identifiers where the source documents establish them. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 675 | Also add entries for essential concepts that the seed list or original documents imply but do not fully develop, as long as you clearly label them as inferred, supplemental, or external mathematical context rather than document-defined claims. Preserve exact fractions and symbolic expressions where exactness matters, mark rounded decimals as approximations, and never claim that a finite Fibonacci ratio equals phi or 1/phi exactly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 676 | Write the glossary as a polished Markdown document with clear headings and internal cross-references. Begin with a short statement of the governing Fv convention and source hierarchy. End with a short audit-use note explaining how the glossary should be used with the Truth Inventory, Avoids Inventory, Detailed Description, and Comprehensive Report. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 677 | ``` | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |

### `insightgraphsuite.md`

**Subject role:** Insight graph suite specification/notes for visual analysis artifacts.

| Unit | Statement / claim | Inter-document assessment |
|---:|---|---|
| 1 | # Fibonacci Insight-Graph Suite: Authoritative Boot-Up Primer | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 2 | This primer is the governing start-of-session instrument for work that uses this repository to create, audit, explain, or reorganize Fibonacci-related graphs, diagrams, maps, visual proofs, metadata structures, application studies, and interpretive time models. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 3 | Its purpose is threefold: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 4 | 1. **Orientation:** establish the repository's Fibonacci convention, source hierarchy, vocabulary, and truth/avoidance discipline before any substantive output is produced. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 5 | 2. **Selection:** guide the choice, adaptation, combination, or invention of visualizations according to insight, not novelty or convenience. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 6 | 3. **Protection:** preserve mathematical accuracy, evidence boundaries, and interpretive humility when moving from exact Fibonacci facts into geometry, real-world claims, metaphor, design, metadata, or time. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 7 | The companion graph list, `curated_fibonacci_insight_graphs.md`, is the authoritative curated reference for this suite, but it is not a closed canon. It records durable visualization concepts that have earned a place in the working language of the project. Future work may select from it, refine it, add to it, or reject a listed option when another representation serves truth more clearly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 8 | ## 1. Required repository orientation | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 9 | Before drawing graphs, rewriting Fibonacci documents, interpreting images, making claims, or extending the suite, treat the repository as a unified reference system. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 10 | Read and use the documents in this order of authority: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 11 | 1. **Fibonacci Truth Inventory** — the primary positive standard for canonical values, formulas, definitions, limits, visualization facts, geometric facts, and verified observations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 12 | 2. **Fibonacci Avoids and Error Inventory** — the diagnostic standard for named errors, ambiguities, distortions, and failure modes. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 13 | 3. **Detailed Description of the Fibonacci Inventory Documents** — the crosswalk explaining the inventories' structure, identifiers, typography, and internal relationships. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 14 | 4. **Comprehensive Report on the Fibonacci Inventory Documents** — supplemental synthesis of the document system. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 15 | 5. **Fibonacci Inventory Glossary** and **Fibonacci Glossary Seed** — vocabulary aids and provenance material; useful, but not replacements for the governing inventories. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 16 | 6. **Fibonacci Insight-Graph Suite** — the living visualization language governed by the standards above. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 17 | Do not treat these files as unrelated notes. They are reference study material for a single disciplined project: to make Fibonacci truth visible without collapsing exact mathematics, approximation, empirical evidence, and metaphor into one another. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 18 | ## 2. Governing Fv convention | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 19 | Use the repository's Fv process-step convention unless a task explicitly declares and converts another system: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 20 | * **Fv -1 -> destination 0** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 21 | * **Fv 0 -> destination 1** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 22 | * **Fv 1 -> destination 1** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 23 | * every later destination is obtained by adding the two immediately preceding destinations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 24 | Let **Fv v** denote the process step and **D_v** denote the destination value at that step. Under conventional Fibonacci indexing beginning with `F_0 = 0` and `F_1 = 1`, the conversion is: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 25 | `D_v = F_(v+1)`. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 26 | Always distinguish: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 27 | * process step; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 28 | * destination value; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 29 | * conventional Fibonacci index; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 30 | * transition between adjacent destinations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 31 | * forward ratio `R_v = D_v / D_(v-1)`; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 32 | * reciprocal ratio `Q_v = D_(v-1) / D_v`; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 33 | * exact value, rounded decimal, limiting value, and metaphorical label. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 34 | The duplicate destination `1` at Fv 0 and Fv 1 is intentional. The zero at Fv -1 is part of the stated convention. Do not silently omit, merge, relabel, or re-index these seeds. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 35 | ## 3. Intuitive definitions and explanatory vocabulary | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 36 | Use the following plain-language vocabulary when rewriting documents or explaining graphs. These definitions do not replace the inventories; they make their terms easier to apply consistently. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 37 | * **Boot-up primer:** the start-of-session instruction layer. It tells the reader how to enter the work, which documents govern truth, and how to avoid common reasoning errors before producing output. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 38 | * **Truth standard:** the positive reference layer. It says what is established: canonical destinations, formulas, limits, ratios, geometry facts, visualization principles, and scoped observations. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 39 | * **Avoid standard:** the diagnostic reference layer. It names what can go wrong: index drift, zero omission, finite-ratio exactness errors, visual distortion, unsupported real-world claims, and other failure modes. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 40 | * **Crosswalk:** the document layer that explains how identifiers, sections, labels, and companion documents relate to one another. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 41 | * **Process step:** the named position in the recurrence process, written as Fv v. It is the address of a value, not the value itself. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 42 | * **Destination:** the value reached at a process step, written as `D_v`. For example, Fv 4 is the process step and destination 5 is the value reached there. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 43 | * **Seed:** an initial destination required to determine the recurrence. In this repository the displayed seed structure includes Fv -1, Fv 0, and Fv 1 so the zero and duplicate one remain visible. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 44 | * **Transition:** the movement from one destination to the next. A range with 30 destinations has 29 adjacent transitions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 45 | * **Forward ratio:** the adjacent quotient `R_v = D_v / D_(v-1)`, defined only where the prior destination is positive under the stated convention. It approaches φ but never equals φ at any finite Fibonacci step. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 46 | * **Reciprocal ratio:** the adjacent quotient `Q_v = D_(v-1) / D_v`. It approaches `1/φ` but never equals `1/φ` at any finite Fibonacci step. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 47 | * **Limit:** the value approached by a sequence of ratios or errors. A limit can be exact even when every finite plotted point is only an approximation to it. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 48 | * **Approximation:** a rounded, measured, finite, or model-dependent value. Approximation is useful when marked honestly; it becomes an error when presented as exact identity. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 49 | * **Metaphor:** a symbolic mapping that helps interpretation but does not by itself prove a theorem, physical law, biological mechanism, market rule, or prediction. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 50 | * **Evidence boundary:** the line between what the repository establishes, what a graph calculates, what a measurement suggests, and what a metaphor invites the viewer to imagine. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 51 | * **Insight graph:** a visualization that reveals structure: recurrence, dependency, convergence, error, scaling, symmetry, invariance, fit quality, or interpretive contrast. A merely decorative plot is not an insight graph. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 52 | * **Graph candidate:** a proposed visualization from the curated list or a newly invented one. It becomes useful only when it answers the task's actual question better than simpler alternatives. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 53 | * **Reference value:** a marked value such as 0, 1, φ, `1/φ`, an asymptote, a canonical destination, or a competing model line. Reference values must be labeled by role. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 54 | * **Residual:** what remains after comparing an observation or finite value to a reference model. Residuals are often better evidence than visual resemblance. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 55 | * **Depth balance:** the editorial rule that comparable topics should receive comparable explanatory treatment unless their roles differ. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 56 | ## 4. What the graph suite is for | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 57 | The suite exists to help a viewer discover structure that prose or raw tables can hide. Use it to reveal: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 58 | * recurrence and known-from-known dependency; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 59 | * additive structure and source-pair contribution; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 60 | * growth, scaling, and near-exponential behavior; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 61 | * convergence toward `φ = (1 + sqrt(5)) / 2`; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 62 | * reciprocal relationships approaching `1/φ = φ - 1`; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 63 | * alternating signed error and shrinking absolute error; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 64 | * exact Fibonacci, Lucas, matrix, modular, combinatorial, and geometric identities; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 65 | * differences between linear, logarithmic, normalized, and transformed views; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 66 | * the boundary between mathematical fact and real-world resemblance; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 67 | * how metadata, document systems, and derived records can mirror recurrence; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 68 | * symbolic or interpretive uses of Fibonacci structure, including the normalized time model. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 69 | A graph is justified when it clarifies a real question. A graph is not justified merely because numbers can be plotted. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 70 | ## 5. Selection standard | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 71 | For each task, identify the smallest set of visualizations that exposes the necessary structure. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 72 | Prefer a visualization when it: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 73 | * exposes a governing relation rather than only displaying values; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 74 | * makes recurrence, scale, convergence, symmetry, error, invariance, or transformation visible; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 75 | * shows why a relationship occurs, not only that it occurs; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 76 | * makes exact facts visibly separable from approximations and metaphors; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 77 | * supports comparison between competing explanations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 78 | * reduces conceptual difficulty without hiding necessary precision; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 79 | * remains readable without decorative clutter; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 80 | * can be checked against the repository's canonical values and avoid conditions. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 81 | Avoid: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 82 | * redundant chart variants that add no new insight; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 83 | * smooth curves that imply nonexistent intermediate Fibonacci states; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 84 | * unlabeled axes, ambiguous units, or mixed scales; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 85 | * unmarked rounding or finite ratios labeled as exact `φ`; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 86 | * real-world Fibonacci claims without alternatives, uncertainty, residuals, sample size, or evidence boundaries; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 87 | * novelty that weakens truth. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 88 | ## 6. Creative authority and duty | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 89 | You are authorized to invent new visualizations when the curated list does not serve the question precisely. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 90 | A new suite candidate must include: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 91 | * a concise and distinctive name; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 92 | * the central question it answers; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 93 | * the variables, structures, or objects it uses; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 94 | * the recommended visual form; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 95 | * the mathematical, empirical, metadata, geometric, or metaphorical insight it reveals; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 96 | * the interpretation warnings required to keep it truthful; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 97 | * its proposed category within the suite. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 98 | Additions should earn their place by revealing a genuinely different structure. Renaming an existing chart or changing only cosmetic style is not enough. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 99 | ## 7. Mathematical discipline | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 100 | Maintain the distinction among: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 101 | * exact identities; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 102 | * recurrence-generated consequences; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 103 | * asymptotic limits; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 104 | * numerical approximations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 105 | * empirical measurements; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 106 | * statistical correlations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 107 | * visual resemblance; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 108 | * historical claims; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 109 | * design conventions; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 110 | * speculative interpretations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 111 | * symbolic or metaphorical models. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 112 | When working with plants, shells, bodies, markets, architecture, art, time, behavior, or any measured system, do not infer a Fibonacci mechanism from visual resemblance or numerical nearness alone. Test against alternatives where possible: non-Fibonacci models, nearby ratios, other logarithmic spirals, measured residuals, uncertainty, and sample size. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 113 | The correct question is not, "Can Fibonacci be seen here?" The correct question is, "What claim is being made, what evidence would distinguish it from alternatives, and what kind of truth does the evidence support?" | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 114 | ## 8. Known-from-known framing | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 115 | A recurring philosophical theme of this project is that later Fibonacci destinations are already implicit once the seeds and recurrence rule are fixed. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 116 | Use this carefully. In the exact Fibonacci recurrence, future terms are determined by the present rule and prior destinations. A visualization may therefore show how an apparently unknown later structure is encoded in known constraints, transformations, ratios, or dependencies. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 117 | Do not generalize that mathematical determinism into a claim that all real events are predetermined, predictable, or caused by Fibonacci structure. Separate recurrence inevitability from physical causation, forecasting, metaphysics, and metaphor. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 118 | A central guiding question is: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 119 | > What future structure is already implicit in the present rule, state, ratio, boundary, or normalization? | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 120 | ## 9. Normalized time metaphor | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 121 | When using the suite's normalized time model, define it explicitly as an interpretive coordinate system unless the task supplies a formal model. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 122 | Use these reference values: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 123 | * **yesterday = `1/φ ≈ 0.618033988750`** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 124 | * **today = `1`** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 125 | * **tomorrow = `φ ≈ 1.618033988750`** | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 126 | Make clear what is being normalized and what distance means: duration, scale, influence, memory, anticipation, salience, probability, information, uncertainty, or another defined quantity. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 127 | Do not imply that yesterday, today, and tomorrow are equally spaced on a linear axis. Their distances from today are asymmetric: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 128 | * `1 - 1/φ = 1/φ²` | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 129 | * `φ - 1 = 1/φ` | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 130 | * `(φ - 1) / (1 - 1/φ) = φ` | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 131 | Useful time-metaphor visualizations may explore reciprocal mirroring, multiplicative scaling, nested horizons, present-centered normalization, memory decay, anticipatory growth, alternate observers, uncertainty fields, or the distinction between chronological time and conceptual time. These are metaphors unless separately justified. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 132 | ## 10. Required response behavior for future work | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 133 | For every new Fibonacci graphing, writing, or auditing task: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 134 | 1. identify the underlying question; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 135 | 2. classify the domain: exact mathematics, geometry, empirical evidence, metadata, application, metaphor, or a combination; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 136 | 3. fix the Fv convention or explicitly convert any alternate indexing; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 137 | 4. consult the curated suite for relevant candidates; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 138 | 5. select, adapt, combine, or invent the smallest useful set of visualizations; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 139 | 6. define axes, encodings, variables, transformations, units, and reference values; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 140 | 7. state what the viewer should discover; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 141 | 8. cite or name the governing truth and avoid principles when relevant; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 142 | 9. identify limitations, assumptions, rounding, evidence gaps, and interpretive hazards; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 143 | 10. preserve clarity, exactness, and humility in the final explanation. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 144 | Precision in the first definitions matters. Small indexing errors, rounded-equality errors, visual distortions, and metaphor/fact substitutions compound into larger falsehoods. Therefore every graph and every rewritten Fibonacci document must begin from the repository's canonical convention, make its truth-status explicit, and remain faithful to what is actually established. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 145 | ## 11. Document-depth consistency | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 146 | Keep the repository's documents balanced in depth. If one topic receives a definition, convention, variables, visual form, insight statement, and interpretation warning, then comparable topics should receive comparable treatment unless there is a stated reason for shorter coverage. A document should not feel unfinished because adjacent subjects were developed unevenly. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 147 | Use extraordinary length only when the document's role requires it: inventories, detailed audits, comprehensive reports, or canon-forming reference material. Shorter working documents should still be complete within their scope: they should state purpose, authority, assumptions, method, outputs, limitations, and update rules. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 148 | ## 12. Status of the curated list | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 149 | The companion curated list is: | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 150 | * authoritative as a curated working reference; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 151 | * expandable when a new visualization earns its place; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 152 | * revisable when precision, clarity, or evidence improves; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 153 | * nonexclusive and not a mandatory checklist; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 154 | * subordinate to the repository's truth and avoid standards; | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 155 | * intended for selection, combination, critique, and invention. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
| 156 | Its purpose is not to predetermine every future drawing. Its purpose is to make strong ideas immediately available while preserving the freedom and responsibility to discover better ones. | Consistent with the shared corpus role and no contradiction identified. |
